Since 5 reps rotate through every store (a visit every ~2.7 days), no store belongs to a single rep, so attribution had to go through visits.\n\n**Finding the signal.** I tested several sales-attribution models — assigning each store-day to the most recent visiting rep (controlling for store baseline, traffic, month, and promotions), an event study around visit dates, product-level sales after each rep's shelf audits, and an out-of-stock channel. Store-level sales turned out to be essentially flat around visits; the per-rep sales signal is far too weak to separate anyone with significance on its own.\n\nThe decisive evidence is in the work-execution data each rep produces. Building a composite score from visit completion rate, planogram compliance, facings, eye-level placement, endcap/checkout displays, promo stands, and POS materials, exactly 10 reps form a cleanly separated cluster: composite z-scores from −2.57 to −1.77, then a gap of 1.45 standard-deviation units to the next rep at −0.31. The group differences are massive (planogram compliance 81.1% vs 86.0%, z = −26; facings 9.46 vs 9.73, t = −18; similar for all display metrics) — and tellingly, it's exactly one rep per region in 10 different regions, ruling out store or regional confounds since their 4 regional peers work the same stores.\n\n**Link to sales.** Shelf state does drive sales in this data: products left compliant or on displays sell ~0.5–1.2% more in the following days.
